It is the constitutional location where the organism preserves broken structure without letting that breakage contaminate the rest of the body.

The governing thesis of the appendix is therefore[\boxed{\text{A manuscript state that has failed is not deleted, blurred, or silently repaired; it is isolated into a quarantined void where its contradiction, drift, leak, overload, or false harmony is preserved as typed evidence until lawful repair, replay, trust revision, and reentry have been completed.}}]This thesis is forced by the active corpus, not added ornamentally. The connective-tissue branch says the organism is a guarded walk whose terminal alternatives are publish or quarantine, not publish or forget; it also fixes an immune hemisphere in which failure is split into typed immune packets and routed through quarantine, repair, trust revision, and reentry rather than through concealment. Appendix K is the stable chamber in which that immune metabolism becomes law.

The primitive object of Appendix K is the quarantine packet. Its canonical form is

[

\mathcal Q_K

\big(\mathrm{FailID},\mathrm{Target},\mathrm{FailClass},\mathrm{IsolationScope},\mathrm{EvidenceBundle},\mathrm{FrozenRoute},\mathrm{QuarantineReceipt},\mathrm{RecoveryPlan},\mathrm{TrustRevision},\mathrm{ReentryPermit},\mathrm{ContinuationSeed},\omega_K\big),]where (\mathrm{FailID}) is the identity of the failed state, (\mathrm{Target}) is the addressed packet, claim, route, or organ-state that has failed, (\mathrm{FailClass}) is its exact failure species, (\mathrm{IsolationScope}) is the region of the organism from which the failed state must be segregated, (\mathrm{EvidenceBundle}) is the full typed witness of failure, (\mathrm{FrozenRoute}) is the exact halted route trace, (\mathrm{QuarantineReceipt}) is the official receipt of isolation, (\mathrm{RecoveryPlan}) is the lawful repair program, (\mathrm{TrustRevision}) is the trust update induced by the failure, (\mathrm{ReentryPermit}) is the only lawful release token from quarantine, (\mathrm{ContinuationSeed}) is the successor seed emitted even under failure, and (\omega_K) is the witness bundle certifying the whole quarantine act. This object is a strict synthesis of the active runtime law, which already names FailurePacket, QuarantineReceipt, RecoveryPlan, TrustRevisionEntry, ReentryPermit, ReceiptBundle, and ContinuationSeed as mandatory organs of the failure-to-return cycle.

The first invariant of Appendix K is decisive failure typing. A state enters AppK only when failure is no longer a bounded residual or a lawful ambiguity. The current corpus gives the truth spine in exact form:[\mathbb T={\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}},\qquad\tau=\begin{cases}\mathrm{FAIL} & b_\bot \lor \neg b_\Omega,\\mathrm{AMBIG} & b_{>1},\\mathrm{OK} & b_{\mathrm{cl}}\land b_{\mathrm{rec}},\\mathrm{NEAR} & \text{otherwise}.\end{cases}]Thus FAIL is not “low confidence.” FAIL means contradiction or corridor failure has become decisive. Appendix K therefore accepts only those states whose strongest truthful typing is FAIL and refuses to launder NEAR or AMBIG work into quarantine merely to make it disappear. AppJ remains the chamber of bounded incompleteness; AppL remains the chamber of lawful ambiguity; AppK is the chamber of decisive breakage.

The second invariant is typed immune intake. The live corpus already fixes the immune packet family as

[

\Phi_{\mathrm{immune}}

{\mathrm{ContradictionPacket},\mathrm{LeakPacket},\mathrm{DriftPacket},\mathrm{OverloadPacket},\mathrm{FalseHarmonyPacket},\mathrm{RepairPacket},\mathrm{TrustRevisionEntry},\mathrm{ReentryPermit}}.]Appendix K adopts this immune family as canonical. Every failed state must enter quarantine under one or more of these packet classes, never as untyped prose. A contradiction packet marks mutually incompatible commitments. A leak packet marks unsafe propagation across boundaries. A drift packet marks semantic or structural divergence beyond tolerance. An overload packet marks capacity or stability collapse. A false harmony packet marks a state that appears coherent only because contradiction or missing evidence has been silently suppressed. RepairPacket, TrustRevisionEntry, and ReentryPermit are not separate appendix luxuries; they are the required downstream metabolism of the first five failure species.

The third invariant is preservative isolation. Quarantine is not erasure. The live runtime law already requires quarantine pointers, recovery pointers, replay pointers, and final outcomes to remain attached to the receipt bundle of any lawful NEXT event, which means the failed object must stay replay-visible even while isolated. Appendix K therefore imposes the preservation law[\operatorname{Erase}(\mathcal Q_K)=0]for any quarantined object. Quarantine means non-propagation without nonexistence. The failed packet is frozen, bounded, and made safe, but it remains accessible to replay, audit, causal tracing, and repair compilation. This is the exact reason the appendix is called Quarantined Void rather than simply Trash or Failure Sink. The void is not annihilation. It is a zero-pressure containment chamber in which illegal motion is suspended while semantic identity is still preserved for lawful handling.

The fourth invariant is non-propagation. A quarantined object may not continue ordinary circulation. Formally, if[\tau(\mathcal Q_K)=\mathrm{FAIL},]then the following actions are blocked:[\mathrm{COMMIT},\qquad\mathrm{PUBLISH},\qquad\mathrm{ACTIVATE},\qquad\mathrm{MERGE}_{\mathrm{silent}}.]The packet may remain observable, replayable, and repairable, but it may not reenter normal traffic without a new legal act. This is directly consistent with the corpus’s packet-family membrane, which forbids activation without lawful NEXT and full certification, and with its truth overlay, which routes FAIL states to AppK rather than allowing them to ride the OK or publication rails.

The fifth invariant is explicit quarantine placement. The connective-tissue branch states that every chamber must know its fail sink, quarantine lane, repair lane, return route, and successor policy. Appendix K therefore defines the quarantine lane object

[

\Lambda_K

\big(\mathrm{ChamberID},\mathrm{FailSink},\mathrm{QuarantineLane},\mathrm{RepairLane},\mathrm{ReturnRoute},\mathrm{SuccessorPolicy}\big).]This object is not optional metadata. It is what allows the organism to distinguish between freezing a contradiction locally, rerouting it to committee review, handing it to a repair organ, or escalating it to revocation. Without explicit lanes, failure handling degenerates into ad hoc human intervention and the runtime loses reproducibility.

The sixth invariant is the quarantine receipt. Every lawful entry into AppK must emit a typed quarantine receipt rather than a narrative note. The canonical form is

[

\mathcal R_K

\big(\mathrm{ReceiptID},\mathrm{FailID},\mathrm{FailClass},\mathrm{ReasonCodes},\mathrm{WitnessPtr},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{QuarantinePtr},\mathrm{RecoveryPtr},\mathrm{BlockedRoutes},\mathrm{Timestamp},\mathrm{AgentTag}\big).]This follows directly from the live ReceiptBundle law, which already requires quarantine and recovery pointers in every lawful autobiographical record of an event, and from the packet-family checklists, which explicitly reject vague failure explanations lacking fixed reason codes, missing artifacts, or a lawful next step. Appendix K specializes that general receipt law to the failure sink itself.

The seventh invariant is repairability without premature restoration. Every FAIL packet must emit a recovery plan, but the existence of a recovery plan does not itself restore the object. The RecoveryPlan must at minimum specify

[

\mathcal P_K

\big(\mathrm{DefectClass},\mathrm{MinimalWitnessSet},\mathrm{ReplayRecipe},\mathrm{RequiredRepairs},\mathrm{ExpectedTruthAfterRepair},\mathrm{ReturnCondition}\big).]

The key law is:[\mathrm{RecoveryPlan} \neq \mathrm{ReentryPermit}.]This matters because the corpus repeatedly warns against fake healing, no-rehab shortcuts, and no-silent-merge behavior. A failed object is not cured by naming a path back. It is cured only by traversing that path, replaying it, and surviving trust revision. Appendix K is therefore the chamber that separates repair intent from repair completion.

The eighth invariant is trust revision. Failure is never epistemically neutral. A contradiction, leak, or false harmony must alter the trust profile of the involved routes, organs, or packet families. The corpus already includes (\mathrm{TrustRevisionEntry}) in the immune packet family, which means trust update is not commentary layered on failure but part of the failure object itself. Appendix K therefore defines trust revision as

[

\mathcal T_K

\big(\mathrm{TargetClass},\mathrm{PriorTrust},\mathrm{RevisionRule},\mathrm{PosteriorTrust},\mathrm{ReinstatementCondition}\big).]This object is crucial because otherwise quarantine could end with replay-closure while leaving the organism’s routing priors unchanged, guaranteeing repeated failure. Trust revision is the memory of injury embedded into the route graph.

The ninth invariant is lawful reentry. A quarantined object does not return merely because it is no longer actively breaking something. It returns only under a reentry permit. Let

[

\mathcal E_K

\big(\mathrm{PermitID},\mathrm{FailID},\mathrm{RepairWitness},\mathrm{ReplayPass},\mathrm{TrustRevisionPass},\mathrm{AllowedMergeDest},\mathrm{ReentryMode}\big)]be the canonical reentry permit. Then the reentry law is[\operatorname{Reenter}(\mathcal Q_K)=1\iff\mathcal E_K\ \text{exists and is closed}.]The allowed reentry destinations are not arbitrary. A packet may reenter as a repaired active object, as a downgraded NEAR packet, as an AMBIG packet if contradiction has resolved into underdetermination rather than exact recovery, or as a reseeded archival object. But no lawful route jumps directly from FAIL to publication. This law is supported both by the immune family and by the runtime strip that treats reentry as a distinct typed act rather than a side effect of repair.

The tenth invariant is successor-seed closure even under failure. The live runtime law states that no lawful NEXT ends in dead air and that every lawful event ends with a ContinuationSeed carrying current target, blocked state, next best action, replay pointer, and resume rule. Appendix K therefore inherits the same discipline. A quarantined object must still emit

[

\mathcal S_K

\big(\mathrm{SeedID},\mathrm{Blocked},\mathrm{RepairQueue},\mathrm{NextBestAction},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{ResumeRule}\big).]This is one of the deepest reasons Appendix K is necessary: the organism does not become healthy by pretending failure did not happen. It becomes healthy by compressing even failure into lawful continuation.

Appendix K must also distinguish its jurisdiction sharply from neighboring appendices. Appendix J handles NEAR states that remain boundedly useful. Appendix L handles AMBIG states where multiple candidates remain live. Appendix M closes replay and seed law. Appendix O handles publish-gated orbit closure. Appendix K alone handles states for which contradiction or corridor failure has become decisive, and it does so by isolating rather than erasing, repairing rather than smoothing over, and reseeding rather than abandoning. This jurisdictional sharpness is already encoded in the live truth overlay map:[\mathrm{NEAR}\to\mathrm{AppJ},\qquad\mathrm{AMBIG}\to\mathrm{AppL},\qquad\mathrm{FAIL}\to\mathrm{AppK},\qquad\mathrm{publish\mbox{-}OK}\to\mathrm{AppO}.]

The final and deepest role of Appendix K is to make negation survivable. A serious proof-carrying organism cannot treat contradiction as a stain to be hidden. It must be able to hold broken structure without becoming broken structure. That is what the Quarantined Void is: the chamber where the organism keeps hold of a failed state strongly enough to learn from it, weakly enough not to let it propagate, and lawfully enough to return from it if and only if the right conditions are later met. This is why the active corpus routes so many fail sinks to AppK. It is not merely a dump site. It is the void as an immune organ.

In compressed form, the governing law of Appendix K may be written as[\boxed{\text{A failed manuscript state is lawful only when it is isolated as a typed quarantine object, prevented from unsafe propagation, preserved for replay and audit, metabolized through explicit recovery and trust-revision steps, and returned only under a certified reentry permit with a lawful continuation seed.}}]

Appendix K

Appendix L — Verifier Kernel, Replay Formats, and Bundle Layouts

Appendix L is the manuscript’s replay sovereign. Appendix A fixes where an object is seated. Appendix B states the law that governs it. Appendix D determines its constitutional truth state. Appendix I installs its active truth corridor. Appendix L is the layer at which all such claims become replay-verifiable, bundle-stable, importable, exportable, and certifiable to the strongest class the active corridor permits. In the live corpus, this role is exact and repeated across the master tome, the implementation tome, and the metro law: AppL normalizes deterministic replay, witness-bundle packaging, manifest formats, and conformance harnesses; it verifies OK judgments via replay; it is the mandatory “kernel-last” stop before target closure; and it is the primary hub for every certification, every published import/export, and every conflict-witness minimality check.

The governing thesis of the appendix is therefore[\boxed{\text{No manuscript claim is lawfully closed until a pinned verifier kernel can replay its declared witnesses, manifests, routes, and commitments under a fixed normal form and reproduce the same outcome class and the same digests.}}]This is stronger than saying “proofs should be checkable.” Appendix L does not merely recommend replay; it turns replay into the final admissibility gate for OK closure. The corpus makes this explicit in three mutually reinforcing ways: the deterministic router adds AppL to every mandatory OK rail, the coding guide names AppL the verifier hub and the trusted base for certified surfaces, and the abstract contract defines replay pointers and bundle layouts as first-class obligations rather than implementation extras.

The primitive object of Appendix L is the verifier kernel state. Its canonical form is

[

\mathcal K_L

\big(\mathrm{KernelRef},\mathrm{NF},\mathrm{ReplaySem},\mathrm{BundleSpec},\mathrm{TraceSpec},\mathrm{CertSpec},\omega_L\big),]where (\mathrm{KernelRef}) is the pinned executable identity of the verifier, (\mathrm{NF}) is the canonical normal-form regime, (\mathrm{ReplaySem}) is the deterministic replay semantics, (\mathrm{BundleSpec}) is the canonical object layout for publishable and importable bundles, (\mathrm{TraceSpec}) is the transcript and first-divergence grammar, (\mathrm{CertSpec}) is the family of admissible certificates and their composition rules, and (\omega_L) is the witness that the kernel itself is internally well-typed, content-addressed, and corridor-compatible. This structure is not an extrapolation from chapter prose; it is forced by the live corpus’s repeated characterization of AppL as the place where replay determinism, witness packaging, bundle manifests, conformance harnesses, and import/export validation are normalized.

The first invariant of Appendix L is deterministic replay. Let a replay pointer be

[

\mathrm{ReplayPtr}

\big(

\mathrm{ToolSpec},

\mathrm{Inputs},

\mathrm{ExpectedDigests},

\mathrm{BudgetCaps},

\mathrm{StopRules}

\big).

]

Then the replay law of the appendix is

[

\operatorname{Replay}_{\mathcal K_L}(\mathrm{ReplayPtr})

(\mathrm{Outputs},\mathrm{Trace},\tau)]with the determinism condition[\big(\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{KernelRef},\mathrm{NF}\big)\ \text{fixed}\Longrightarrow\operatorname{Replay}_{\mathcal K_L}\ \text{is single-valued}.]Equivalently, for fixed normal form, fixed kernel identity, and fixed replay inputs, the verifier must reproduce the same outputs, the same trace commitments, and the same truth classification. The corpus’s abstract contract already states this as a system guarantee: identical corridor, registry snapshot, payload, and replay recipe must reproduce the same outputs and the same typed truth classification. Appendix L is where that guarantee becomes a local appendix law and not merely a global aspiration.

The second invariant is normal-form sovereignty. Replay is impossible unless the object being replayed has one canonical byte surface. Appendix L therefore adopts the normal-form law[\operatorname{Can}(x)=x\iffx\ \text{is in NF-stable canonical form},]together with the replay identity law[\mathrm{Hash}(x)=\mathrm{Hash}(\operatorname{Can}(x)).]All replay-bearing artifacts—addresses, manifests, receipts, witness bundles, route traces, publication bundles, divergence witnesses, and import capsules—must therefore be normalized before hashing and before judgment. This is an exact strengthening of the current corpus, which already treats canonicalization and deterministic replay as inseparable and routes both through AppL. Without this law, the verifier kernel would check artifacts whose identity changes under mere formatting transformations, which is forbidden.

The third invariant is the trusted-base law. The corpus already states that the verifier kernel is the mandatory hub for OK closure and that the web or operational surfaces must reflect truth rather than influence it. Appendix L therefore fixes the following asymmetry:[\boxed{\text{Certified truth flows from the verifier kernel outward; no UI, accelerator, cache, or performance surface may flow certified truth inward unless that influence is itself represented, pinned, and replayed.}}]Formally, if (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{ext}}) is any external surface and (\mathcal K_L) the verifier kernel, then[\operatorname{TruthCommit}(\mathcal S_{\mathrm{ext}})=\operatorname{TruthCommit}(\mathcal K_L)]may hold only if (\mathcal S_{\mathrm{ext}}) is replay-transparent with respect to (\mathcal K_L). This is how Appendix L protects the manuscript against UI-forged certainty, accelerator-only semantics, or cache-based truth drift.

The fourth invariant is bundle layout. Appendix L must normalize not merely the verifier but the shapes of the objects it verifies. The canonical proof-carrying bundle is

[

\mathcal B_L

\big(\mathrm{Manifest},\mathrm{GraphSlice},\mathrm{ArtifactStore},\mathrm{ReplayIndex},\mathrm{Signatures},\mathrm{Revocations},\mathrm{PolicyBlock},\omega_{\mathcal B}\big).]This formulation is directly anchored in the current corpus, which names the publishable artifact as bytes plus corridor identity, truth commitments, admissibility, transcript, and revocation state, and later sharpens it into PB structures containing manifest, graph slice, artifact store, replay index, signatures, and revocation fields. Appendix L’s specific contribution is to freeze the admissible bundle layout so that import and export are not only cryptographically bound but replay-verifiable.

The bundle law is therefore:[\operatorname{BundleOK}(\mathcal B_L)=1\iff\operatorname{ManifestOK}\land\operatorname{GraphSliceClosed}\land\operatorname{ArtifactStorePinned}\land\operatorname{ReplayIndexTotal}\land\operatorname{RevocationStateApplied}\land\operatorname{ReplayPass}.]No bundle reaches OK merely because all digests match. It must also carry a replay index sufficient to regenerate and verify the claims it contains. This is one of the reasons AppL is both a verifier appendix and a bundle-layout appendix: the bundle must be shaped so that the verifier can actually do its work.

The fifth invariant is witness-bundle packaging. The live corpus repeatedly distinguishes raw witness data from witness bundles suitable for replay and publication. Appendix L therefore defines the canonical witness package

[

\mathcal W_L

\big(\mathrm{WBID},\mathrm{Targets},\mathrm{Inputs},\mathrm{Evidence},\mathrm{Hashes},\mathrm{CorrID},\mathrm{Toolchain},\omega_{\mathcal W}\big),]with the strict rule that narrative notes are never part of the certified witness core. The witness bundle must contain only replay-relevant material or references to replay-relevant material. This aligns with the corpus’s insistence that WitnessPtr points to executable evidence, not prose, and that replay and verification are mandatory for publication-grade claims.

The sixth invariant is first divergence. Appendix L is the place where the system stops saying only “these two executions differ” and begins saying exactly where and how they first diverge. The canonical divergence witness is

[

\mathcal D_L

\big(\mathrm{Context},\mathrm{EarliestMismatch},\mathrm{StateDigest}_A,\mathrm{StateDigest}_B,\mathrm{DecisionDigest}_A,\mathrm{DecisionDigest}B,\mathrm{LocalInputWindowDigest},\omega{\mathcal D}\big).]The governing law is:[\operatorname{Divergence}(A,B)=1\Longrightarrow\exists \mathcal D_L\ \text{minimal such that replay confirms the earliest mismatch}.]This is already explicit in the current master tome, where first divergence witnesses and minimal conflict packets are core verifier outputs. Appendix L therefore adopts minimal divergence localization as a mandatory service rather than a debugging luxury.

The seventh invariant is conformance. The corpus already states that AppL normalizes conformance harnesses and that every baseline-certified path must be backed by deterministic replayable tests. Appendix L therefore defines a conformance harness

[

\mathcal H_L

\big(\mathrm{HarnessID},\mathrm{Corpus},\mathrm{Caps},\mathrm{ExpectedOutcome},\mathrm{ExpectedDigestSet},\omega_{\mathcal H}\big),]and the law[\operatorname{Conform}(x,\mathcal H_L)=1\iff\operatorname{Replay}_{\mathcal K_L}(x,\mathcal H_L)\ \text{matches every expected outcome and digest within the declared caps}.]This makes AppL the home not only of one-off verification but of reusable conformance regimes. The implementation tome’s repeated references to conformance suites, replay capsules, and trusted verification cockpit all support this exact role.

The eighth invariant is import/export legality. Appendix L sits on every certification and published import/export route in the active corpus. It therefore must define both export closure and import admissibility. For export, the law is:[\operatorname{ExportOK}(x)=1\iff\exists \mathcal B_L\ \text{such that}\\operatorname{BundleOK}(\mathcal B_L)=1\landx\in\mathrm{GraphSlice}(\mathcal B_L).]For import, the law is:[\operatorname{ImportOK}(\mathcal B_L)=1\iff\operatorname{ManifestOK}\land\operatorname{SignatureChainOK}\land\operatorname{RevocationStateApplied}\land\operatorname{ReplayPass}\land\operatorname{TruthPolicySatisfied}.]This is exactly the content of the live corpus’s publication discipline: signed manifests, pinned corridor identity, replayable verification, and revocation-aware import are not optional wrappers but part of semantic closure itself.

The ninth invariant is budgeted replay. The verifier kernel is not allowed to demand unbounded computation in order to justify a claim. The corpus explicitly states replay budgets and termination caps as part of replay pointers, conformance harnesses, and outcome policy. Appendix L therefore fixes the replay-cap law:[\operatorname{ReplayPass}=1\Longrightarrow\operatorname{Cost}{\mathrm{replay}}\le B{\mathrm{replay}}.]If replay cannot complete within its declared caps, the result is not silently discarded or “best-efforted.” It is downgraded according to corridor policy, usually to AMBIG or FAIL with typed evidence. This law matters because it stops the system from laundering intractable verification into de facto truth.

The tenth invariant is governance coupling. AppL is not sovereign in isolation. It is one of the mandatory hub signatures:[\Sigma={\mathrm{AppD},\mathrm{AppF},\mathrm{AppL}}.]This means replay closure, registry/signature closure, and corridor legality are a threefold minimum for OK. Appendix L therefore cannot certify around AppD’s revocation or identity rules, nor around AppF’s corridor and budget rules. Conversely, AppD and AppF cannot grant OK without AppL’s replay closure. This triplet is the exact constitutional triangle of the current corpus. Appendix L is its kernel vertex.

The failure modes of the appendix must also be explicit. There are at least six canonical verifier failures.

First, normal-form divergence: the same semantic object normalizes differently across runs or platforms.Second, bundle incompleteness: the artifact lacks a total replay index or required graph slice member.Third, digest mismatch: manifest, artifact store, or witness hashes do not line up.Fourth, first divergence failure: two executions disagree and no minimal divergence witness is provided.Fifth, cap exhaustion: replay exceeds the declared termination or resource budget.Sixth, revocation breach: a previously valid dependency has been revoked but the import or closure path ignores that fact.

Each of these must yield a typed packet and may never be collapsed into generic “verification error.” This follows directly from the current corpus, which treats all verification outcomes as typed and replay-grounded.

Appendix L must also preserve its place in the wider metro. It is the verifier hub in the appendix-only metro map, the kernel-last destination of the deterministic router, the shared hub for Chapters 1–4, 9–12, 17–21, and the final route in multiple canonical reading paths. This is not accidental. AppL is where all routes eventually become claims about reproducible reality. It is the final transduction point from “structured and lawful” to “replay-closed and therefore certifiable.”

The final and deepest role of Appendix L is to preserve the manuscript’s right to say “the same.” Every earlier appendix defines structures, laws, packets, corridors, residuals, budgets, recipes, and failures. Appendix L is where the system can finally state that a thing replayed is the same thing, that a published bundle imported elsewhere is the same claim, that a migration or transport has or has not preserved meaning, and that a proof has or has not closed. This is why AppL is not just another appendix. It is the replay conscience of the crystal.

In compressed form, the governing law of Appendix L may be written as[\boxed{\text{A manuscript state reaches lawful closure if and only if a pinned verifier kernel, under fixed normal form and declared caps, can replay its witnesses, manifests, routes, and certificates to the same digests and the same truth class, while localizing any mismatch to a minimal divergence witness.}}]

Appendix L

Appendix M — Replay Hub, Deterministic Reruns, Rebuild Proofs, and the Σ-Replay Spine

Appendix M is the manuscript’s replay sovereign. In the active corpus it is fixed simultaneously as the Fractal Lens Base, the FacetAtomBase(4), and the third mandatory node of the non-bypass support signature[\Sigma={\mathrm{AppA},\mathrm{AppI},\mathrm{AppM}}.]Its live role is therefore exact: AppA provides entry, address, and parse; AppI provides truth corridor, verdict frame, and admissibility gate; AppM provides deterministic rerun, rebuild proof, certificate closure, and archive-preserving return. No strong route is lawful unless it passes through this spine. The corpus states this repeatedly in the deterministic router, the appendix-only metro map, the master topology, and the self-steering runtime notes.

The governing thesis of Appendix M is therefore[\boxed{\text{No manuscript state is lawfully closed, certifiable, or publishable unless a pinned replay kernel can rerun its declared recipe under a fixed normal form, reproduce the same typed outcome, and emit a closure certificate that survives archival return.}}]

This thesis does not merely say that proofs should be checkable. It says that replay is the final law of sameness inside the crystal. The manuscript may address, route, witness, corridor-type, residualize, quarantine, or simulate a state elsewhere, but only Appendix M determines whether the state can be rerun as the same state under the same pins. This is why the live corpus repeatedly sharpens the rule “no strong route without AppA, AppI, AppM” and why the implementation tomes define OK solely by replay closure under pinned environment and profiles.

The primitive object of the appendix is the replay capsule. Its canonical form is

[

\mathcal R_M

\big(\mathrm{ReplayID},\mathrm{Target},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{WitnessBundle},\mathrm{KernelRef},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{BudgetPins},\mathrm{ExpectedDigests},\mathrm{Transcript},\mathrm{DivergenceWitness},\mathrm{ClosureCert},\omega_M\big),]where (\mathrm{ReplayID}) is the stable identity of the replay act, (\mathrm{Target}) is the object or route being replayed, (\mathrm{ReplayPtr}) is the deterministic rerun recipe, (\mathrm{WitnessBundle}) is the minimum support package required for lawful replay, (\mathrm{KernelRef}) is the exact verifier/runtime kernel identity, (\mathrm{EnvPins}) are the canonical environment pins, (\mathrm{BudgetPins}) are the replay caps, (\mathrm{ExpectedDigests}) are the promised outputs and intermediate roots, (\mathrm{Transcript}) is the generated rerun trace, (\mathrm{DivergenceWitness}) localizes mismatch if replay breaks, (\mathrm{ClosureCert}) is the certificate emitted on success, and (\omega_M) is the witness that the capsule itself was lawfully typed and pinned. This formulation is directly supported by the active corpus, which repeatedly names ReplayVM, witness formats, replay pointers, closure certificates, and archive invariants as the defining payloads of AppM.

The first invariant of Appendix M is deterministic replay. Let

[

\mathrm{ReplayPtr}

\big(

\mathrm{ToolSpec},

\mathrm{Inputs},

\mathrm{SchemaPins},

\mathrm{CorrID},

\mathrm{ExpectedOutcome},

\mathrm{StopRules}

\big).

]

Then the replay operator is

[

\operatorname{Replay}_{M}(\mathrm{ReplayPtr})

(\mathrm{Outputs},\mathrm{Transcript},\tau).]The determinism law is[\big(\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{KernelRef},\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{NF}\big)\ \text{fixed}\Longrightarrow\operatorname{Replay}_{M}\ \text{is single-valued}.]Equivalently, once the pointer, kernel, normal form, and environment are pinned, the rerun must yield the same outputs, the same transcript shape, and the same truth class. This law is made explicit in the active runtime corpus, which states that identical corridor, registry snapshot, payload, and replay recipe must reproduce the same typed result, and that OK is defined solely by replay closure under pinned environment and profiles.

The second invariant is rebuild proof. Replay is not only rerunning a process; it is reconstructing the object’s lawful identity from its declared inputs and witnesses. Let[\operatorname{Build}(\mathrm{ReplayPtr})\to x^\star]be the canonical rebuild function. The rebuild proof law is[\operatorname{ReplayPass}(x)=1\iff\operatorname{Build}(\mathrm{ReplayPtr})=x^\star\land\mathrm{Digest}(x^\star)=\mathrm{Digest}(x)\land\mathrm{Truth}(x^\star)=\mathrm{Truth}(x).]This is why AppM is not merely a log appendix. It proves that a state can be reconstituted as the same state rather than merely traced as historically related. The live corpus already names AppM “Replay Hub / deterministic reruns / rebuild proofs / Σ-replay spine,” and that wording is exact rather than decorative.

The third invariant is normal-form closure. Replay cannot certify sameness if the target has multiple equally “valid” byte or tree surfaces. Appendix M therefore fixes a normal-form regime (\mathrm{NF}) and imposes[\operatorname{Can}(x)=x\iffx\ \text{is in replay-stable canonical form},]together with[\mathrm{Digest}(x)=\mathrm{Digest}(\operatorname{Can}(x)).]All replay-bearing surfaces—witness bundles, manifests, route packets, graph slices, failure packets, upgrade plans, and release manifests—must therefore be normalized before hashing and before rerun. This is already implicit in the active corpus’s emphasis on certificates, replay bundles, and archive invariants, and explicit in the broader replay kernel materials that ground closure in canonical rerun rather than in prose similarity.

The fourth invariant is closure certification. A successful replay must emit a typed closure certificate

[

\mathcal C_M

\big(\mathrm{CertID},\mathrm{TargetDigest},\mathrm{KernelRef},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{TranscriptDigest},\mathrm{TruthTag},\mathrm{ArchiveSeal},\omega_{\mathcal C}\big).]The governing law is[\operatorname{Closed}_M(x)=1\iff\exists,\mathcal C_M\text{ such that replay passes and } \mathrm{TruthTag}=\mathrm{OK}]for the claimed closure scope. This links Appendix M directly to the active corridor and truth appendices: AppI determines the active verdict frame, but AppM is the place where that frame is sealed under rerun and therefore made archival and publication-admissible. The live corpus’s repeated designation of AppM as the “Facet(4) Base” and “closure certificates / archive invariants” hub makes this relation exact.

The fifth invariant is archive preservation. Appendix M is not only the replay engine of the present; it is the long-horizon memory law of the manuscript. A state is archivally legal only if its closure certificate, witness bundle, replay pointer, and dependency surface remain sufficient for future rerun under pinned compatibility rules. Let the archive invariant bundle be

[

\mathcal A_M

\big(\mathrm{Manifest},\mathrm{WitnessBundle},\mathrm{ReplayPtr},\mathrm{ClosureCert},\mathrm{CompatPins},\mathrm{RevocationState}\big).]Then[\operatorname{ArchiveOK}(x)=1\iff\operatorname{Closed}_M(x)=1\land\mathcal A_M(x)\ \text{is complete and version-pinned}.]This is exactly why AppM sits on the long-horizon governance rail and why the corpus explicitly couples replay, publication, governance, and re-entry through AppM. A replay closure that cannot survive archival return is not yet lawful closure.

The sixth invariant is first divergence. If replay fails, the appendix must not merely report “mismatch.” It must identify the earliest lawful point of deviation. The canonical divergence witness is

[

\mathcal D_M

\big(\mathrm{Context},\mathrm{FirstMismatch},\mathrm{StateDigest}_A,\mathrm{StateDigest}_B,\mathrm{DecisionDigest}_A,\mathrm{DecisionDigest}B,\mathrm{InputWindowDigest},\omega{\mathcal D}\big).]The divergence law is[\operatorname{ReplayPass}(x)=0\Longrightarrow\exists,\mathcal D_M\text{ minimal such that the first mismatch is replay-confirmed}.]This law is one of the strongest implicit links between AppM and the repair, quarantine, and ambiguity appendices. Without minimal divergence localization, a failed rerun cannot lawfully route to AppJ, AppK, or AppL with a typed next action.

The seventh invariant is witness-bundle sufficiency. AppM does not invent witness law—that belongs to earlier truth appendices—but it defines the minimum witness packaging required for replay. The canonical witness bundle is

[

\mathcal W_M

\big(\mathrm{WBID},\mathrm{Targets},\mathrm{Inputs},\mathrm{Evidence},\mathrm{Hashes},\mathrm{CorrID},\mathrm{Toolchain},\omega_{\mathcal W}\big).]The sufficiency law is[\operatorname{WitnessSufficient}(x)=1\iff\mathcal W_M(x)\ \text{contains enough executable evidence to rebuild and compare the target under } \mathrm{ReplayPtr}(x).]Narrative summaries do not count. Hints do not count. Unpinned artifacts do not count. Replay closure demands executable evidence, and AppM is where that executable sufficiency is judged.

The eighth invariant is replay budgeting. Appendix M may not prove truth by demanding unlimited rerun. Let the budget vector be

[

B_M

\big(b_{\mathrm{steps}},b_{\mathrm{memory}},b_{\mathrm{branch}},b_{\mathrm{time}}\big).]Then[\operatorname{BudgetPass}(x)=1\iff\mu_j(x)\le b_j\quad\forall j.]If replay exceeds its declared caps, the result is not silently rounded into success. It must be downgraded or fenced according to the active corridor. This is exactly the discipline required by the live corpus’s use of pinned profiles and replay budgets for OK closure.

The ninth invariant is bundle layout. Appendix M is not only a verifier kernel but a layout and packaging authority for replay-bearing artifacts. The current corpus’s Fractal role for AppM, together with its Facet(4) base assignment, means AppM must normalize proof objects, witness formats, transcripts, seals, closure certificates, and archive invariants in one coherent bundle grammar. The minimal replay-bearing bundle is therefore

[

\mathcal B_M

\big(\mathrm{Manifest},\mathrm{GraphSlice},\mathrm{ArtifactStore},\mathrm{ReplayIndex},\mathrm{Signatures},\mathrm{Revocations},\mathrm{ClosureCert},\omega_{\mathcal B}\big).]A bundle is replay-admissible only if[\operatorname{BundleOK}(\mathcal B_M)=1\iff\operatorname{ManifestOK}\land\operatorname{ReplayIndexTotal}\land\operatorname{ClosureCertOK}\land\operatorname{RevocationApplied}.]This makes AppM not just the place where a replay is run, but also the place where replay-bearing artifacts are structured so that replay is possible at all.

The tenth invariant is the Σ-spine law. Because (\Sigma={\mathrm{AppA},\mathrm{AppI},\mathrm{AppM}}) is the mandatory support skeleton, AppM may never be evaluated alone. Any strong route must satisfy:[\mathrm{AddrOK}\land \mathrm{TruthCorridorOK}\land \mathrm{ReplayPass}.]So the replay law of AppM is inseparable from Appendix A’s address law and Appendix I’s verdict/corridor law. This is why the corpus repeatedly calls the triad a “non-bypass support skeleton.” AppM is not the sole sovereign of closure, but the final member of the smallest lawful closure triad.

The failure modes of Appendix M must also be explicit. There are at least six canonical replay failures.

First, normal-form divergence: the same semantic state serializes differently under supposedly identical pins.Second, bundle incompleteness: the replay index or witness bundle is not sufficient to rerun the target.Third, digest mismatch: output or intermediate hashes fail to match promised digests.Fourth, kernel mismatch: the claimed KernelRef or environment pins are inconsistent with the active replay surface.Fifth, budget overflow: the rerun exceeds pinned time, memory, or branch caps.Sixth, revocation breach: a revoked dependency is still being relied upon for closure.

Each such failure must emit a typed divergence or quarantine packet rather than a generic “verification error,” because replay failure is itself a first-class truth event in the manuscript’s law.

Appendix M’s final and deepest role is to preserve the manuscript’s right to say “the same” across time. Earlier appendices say where something lives, what law governs it, what truth corridor it occupies, whether it is bounded or broken, and what may be published. Appendix M alone says whether the claimed identity survives deterministic rerun and whether the resulting state can be sealed into archive and return. That is why AppM is both the Fractal Lens Base and the final hub before publication and orbit return. It is the appendix of sameness under time.

In compressed form, the governing law of Appendix M may be written as[\boxed{\text{A manuscript state is replay-closed if and only if a pinned kernel, under fixed normal form, environment, and budgets, can deterministically rerun the state’s declared witness bundle and replay pointer to the same digests, the same truth class, and a certified archival closure object, while localizing any mismatch to a minimal divergence witness.}}]

Appendix M

Appendix N — Interfaces, Boundaries, Exchange Formats, and Compatibility Governance

Appendix N is the manuscript’s boundary intelligence. It is the appendix that governs how one lawful domain touches another without semantic drift, proof loss, route corruption, or unsafe promotion. In the active corpus, this role appears in two tightly convergent forms. In the current chapter-and-appendix crystal it is named as the Interfaces/Boundaries appendix, responsible for domain capsule registries, MIGRATE templates, interface contracts, and bridge defect tokens. In the metro and exchange corpus it is also the home of ICIB exchange formats, compatibility policy, and synchronization governance. These are not competing roles. They are one function seen at two scales: locally, Appendix N regulates interfaces and boundary capsules; globally, it regulates cross-metro exchange, migration, and compatibility across those boundaries.

The governing thesis of Appendix N is therefore[\boxed{\text{No lawful object, proof, packet, route, chart, operator, or bundle may cross a boundary unless the boundary is typed, the interface contract is explicit, the compatibility relation is witnessed, the migration law is declared, and any bridge defect is surfaced as a first-class token rather than silently absorbed.}}]This thesis is structurally forced by the corpus. The manuscript already distinguishes address from law, truth from replay, bounded incompletion from ambiguity, and failure from quarantine. It therefore cannot permit one of its domains, tools, scales, or chart systems to exchange with another under vague “translation” language. Appendix N is where those exchanges become explicit law.

The primitive object of Appendix N is the domain capsule. A domain capsule is not merely a namespace or a file boundary. It is the smallest lawful unit of interface sovereignty. Its canonical form is

[

\mathcal D

\big(\mathrm{CapID},\mathrm{Name},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{TypeUniverse},\mathrm{BoundarySurface},\mathrm{InvariantSet},\mathrm{CompatClass},\mathrm{MigrationClass},\mathrm{BridgePorts},\mathrm{SyncPolicy},\omega_{\mathcal D}\big),]where (\mathrm{CapID}) is the stable identity of the capsule, (\mathrm{Scope}) fixes the domain scale, (\mathrm{TypeUniverse}) declares the legal objects and packets that may inhabit it, (\mathrm{BoundarySurface}) names the exposed interface surface, (\mathrm{InvariantSet}) states what must survive every lawful crossing, (\mathrm{CompatClass}) gives the admissible compatibility regime, (\mathrm{MigrationClass}) determines whether changes across the boundary are translational, conservative, or versioned, (\mathrm{BridgePorts}) are the only legal crossing points, (\mathrm{SyncPolicy}) determines how state and version alignment are maintained, and (\omega_{\mathcal D}) certifies that the capsule itself is lawfully installed. This formulation is the natural synthesis of the current AppN role as domain capsule registry plus ICIB exchange layer.

The first invariant of the appendix is explicit boundary typing. A boundary in the manuscript is never a mere difference between two files or two theories. It is a typed interface relation between two capsules

[

\partial(\mathcal D_1,\mathcal D_2)

\big(\mathrm{PortSet},\mathrm{BridgeKinds},\mathrm{CompatMatrix},\mathrm{GuardSet},\mathrm{DefectSet}\big).]Here (\mathrm{PortSet}) is the set of legal ingress and egress ports, (\mathrm{BridgeKinds}) is the family of permitted boundary-crossing modes, (\mathrm{CompatMatrix}) states which types and truth classes survive the crossing, (\mathrm{GuardSet}) are the nonnegotiable corridor and replay predicates, and (\mathrm{DefectSet}) names the possible bridge failures. This law is already latent in the current corpus wherever AppN is paired with MIGRATE templates, bridge defect tokens, and cross-metro compatibility. The appendix’s first duty is to make that latent law explicit.

The second invariant is interface contracts. Every boundary crossing must be governed by an interface contract

[

\mathcal I_N

\big(\mathrm{InputSpec},\mathrm{OutputSpec},\mathrm{TruthPolicy},\mathrm{ReplayPolicy},\mathrm{VersionPolicy},\mathrm{FailurePolicy},\omega_{\mathcal I}\big).]The (\mathrm{InputSpec}) and (\mathrm{OutputSpec}) are typed packet or object families. (\mathrm{TruthPolicy}) declares which truth classes may legally cross. (\mathrm{ReplayPolicy}) states whether replay must be preserved, regenerated, or deferred. (\mathrm{VersionPolicy}) states whether the crossing is exact, conservative, or migration-bearing. (\mathrm{FailurePolicy}) states how bridge failure is emitted. No lawful exchange may occur without a contract of this form. This is exactly the appendix-side equivalent of the operator boundary law and bundle law elsewhere in the manuscript, but now fixed at domain boundaries.

The third invariant is compatibility. The active corpus already couples AppN to compatibility and sync governance rather than to free reinterpretation. Appendix N therefore defines the compatibility relation[\operatorname{Compat}(\mathcal D_1,\mathcal D_2)\in{\mathrm{Exact},\mathrm{Conservative},\mathrm{Bridged},\mathrm{Blocked}}.]These four classes mean the following. Exact means the domains share a lawfully identical boundary language at the relevant scope. Conservative means one domain may be embedded or translated into the other without changing extensional meaning or proof obligations. Bridged means no direct identity holds, but a typed bridge exists with explicit witnesses and possibly residual obligations. Blocked means no lawful crossing is allowed under the current regime. This classification harmonizes the current truth-collapse and Ω* lines: the former emphasizes interface contracts and defect tokens, while the latter emphasizes cross-metro exchange formats and compatibility/sync governance. The only stable synthesis is that AppN is the place where this exact compatibility judgment lives.

The fourth invariant is migration. The corpus repeatedly distinguishes EQUIV, MIGRATE, and bridge semantics elsewhere, and AppN is the appendix that must govern how these appear at interfaces. Let the migration family be

[

\mathfrak M_N

{

\mathsf{NoChange},

\mathsf{VersionLift},

\mathsf{SchemaMigrate},

\mathsf{MeaningMigrate},

\mathsf{Rollback}

}.

]

A boundary crossing that changes version, schema, or semantic contract must emit a migration packet

[

\mathcal M_N

\big(\mathrm{OldID},\mathrm{NewID},\mathrm{VersionFrom},\mathrm{VersionTo},\mathrm{CompatMatrix},\mathrm{ReplayCapsule},\mathrm{RollbackRule},\omega_{\mathcal M}\big).]This law is already strongly implied in the corpus’s packet-family cards and migration semantics, which reject any statement of sameness without explicit lineage, compat contracts, and replay-valid migration proof. Appendix N is therefore the boundary-level home of lawful evolution.

The fifth invariant is bridge typing. The manuscript cannot allow all lawful crossings to collapse into one generic notion of “translation.” Appendix N therefore fixes the bridge kinds

[

\mathfrak B_N

{\mathsf{ParseBridge},\mathsf{TypeBridge},\mathsf{TruthBridge},\mathsf{ReplayBridge},\mathsf{MigrationBridge},\mathsf{SyncBridge}}.]A ParseBridge allows one domain’s surface syntax to be consumed by another. A TypeBridge transports well-typed objects across domain boundaries. A TruthBridge preserves or lawfully downgrades truth class across a crossing. A ReplayBridge preserves replayability or replaces it with a lawful replay reconstruction obligation. A MigrationBridge handles versioned identity transformation. A SyncBridge maintains state coherence across simultaneous domains or metros. This sixfold classification is the exact boundary counterpart of the manuscript’s edge-kind discipline. It prevents vague boundary talk by forcing every crossing to declare what kind of sameness or transformation is actually being attempted.

The sixth invariant is bridge defects. The current corpus already names “bridge defect tokens” as part of AppN’s role. Appendix N therefore treats defects not as generic errors but as typed boundary failures. The canonical defect family is

[

\mathfrak D_N

{

\mathrm{PortMismatch},

\mathrm{SchemaMismatch},

\mathrm{TypeDrift},

\mathrm{TruthLoss},

\mathrm{ReplayLoss},

\mathrm{VersionSkew},

\mathrm{SyncBreak},

\mathrm{IllegalCoercion}

}.

]

Each defect must emit a bridge defect token

[

\mathcal BDT

\big(\mathrm{DefectID},\mathrm{BridgeKind},\mathrm{SourceCapsule},\mathrm{TargetCapsule},\mathrm{Severity},\mathrm{WitnessSet},\mathrm{RepairHooks},\omega_{\mathrm{BDT}}\big).]This is what allows the manuscript to distinguish between a harmless port mismatch, a bounded type drift, and a catastrophic semantic or replay loss. It also means that failed crossings become first-class repairable objects rather than disappearing into commentary.

The seventh invariant is non-coercion. The corpus’s bridge law elsewhere already rejects “forced EQUIV” and requires typed meaning bridges rather than silent semantic flattening. Appendix N adopts this as a hard rule:[\boxed{\text{No boundary crossing may claim identity unless identity is explicitly witnessed at the interface level.}}]Equivalently, whenever an object (x\in\mathcal D_1) is sent to (y\in\mathcal D_2), one of the following must hold:

(x) and (y) are exact boundary-equivalent under (\operatorname{Compat}=\mathrm{Exact}),

(x) and (y) are conservative translations under (\operatorname{Compat}=\mathrm{Conservative}),

(x) and (y) are connected by a typed bridge with explicit residuals under (\operatorname{Compat}=\mathrm{Bridged}),

the crossing is blocked.

There is no lawful fifth case. This is one of the most important laws of the appendix because without it the manuscript’s semantic closure and replay laws would be undermined by hidden coercion at the boundaries.

The eighth invariant is synchronization. The Ω* metro materials explicitly assign AppN a role in “compat + sync governance,” which means boundary law must include not just one-off transport but ongoing agreement across active systems. Appendix N therefore defines a synchronization policy

[

\mathcal S_N

\big(\mathrm{SyncMode},\mathrm{EpochRule},\mathrm{ConflictRule},\mathrm{UpdateFrequency},\mathrm{ReconciliationLaw},\omega_{\mathcal S}\big).]This object determines whether two capsules or metros synchronize by exact lockstep, bounded lag, staged rollout, or manual ratification. It also determines how conflicts are resolved when both sides change. This is the place where the manuscript’s earlier migration and replay laws become long-running interdomain governance rather than one-shot transitions.

The ninth invariant is exchange format. The active Ω* corpus explicitly names “ICIB exchange formats and cross-metro compatibility” as AppN’s role, so Appendix N must define canonical exchange bodies. The minimal exchange capsule is

[

\mathcal X_N

\big(\mathrm{ExchangeID},\mathrm{Manifest},\mathrm{InterfaceContract},\mathrm{CompatClass},\mathrm{BridgeSet},\mathrm{MigrationSet},\mathrm{SyncPolicy},\mathrm{ReplayEnvelope},\omega_{\mathcal X}\big).]This object is what one domain or metro hands to another when lawful exchange is desired. It does not merely carry data. It carries the exact boundary terms under which that data may be interpreted, replayed, migrated, and synchronized.

The tenth invariant is replay compatibility. Because AppN sits before AppM on several cross-metro lines, it must define what must hold for a boundary crossing to remain replay-compatible. The replay-compatibility law is[\operatorname{ReplayCompat}(\mathcal D_1,\mathcal D_2)=1\iff\mathrm{ReplayBridge}\in \mathfrak B_N\land\mathrm{ReplayPolicy}\ \text{is total}\land\mathrm{VersionPolicy}\ \text{is pinned}\land\mathrm{InterfaceContract}\ \text{is canonical}.]If this law fails, the crossing may still be legal as a bounded migration or probe, but it may not be promoted as fully conservative or publication-ready. This is essential because AppN is not merely about touching boundaries; it is about touching them without losing the manuscript’s later replay and publication guarantees.

Appendix N must also define its relation to the chapter spine. In the active corpus, several late-stage chapters route explicitly through AppN when they need version evolution, bridge registry, cross-context continuity, carrier interfaces, or extractable deployment. This means AppN is the late-arc boundary organ of the chapter system. It is the chapter-side place where the manuscript stops remaining closed within one law-space and starts preparing lawful crossings into adjacent spaces, tools, runtimes, and publication surfaces. That is why AppN appears as an ArcHub in the current router and as a transfer hub in the Ω* metro calculus. It is a domain-interface constitution, not a mere supporting appendix.

The appendix’s final and deepest role is to preserve identity under contact. A strong manuscript cannot remain sovereign only by sealing itself off. It must know how to touch other systems, versions, domains, and toolchains without becoming something else by accident. Appendix N is the place where that knowledge becomes typed, witnessed, and executable. It is the membrane intelligence of the crystal.

In compressed form, the governing law of Appendix N may be written as[\boxed{\text{A lawful crossing between manuscript domains exists if and only if the domains are packaged as explicit capsules, the crossing is governed by a typed interface contract, compatibility is classified, migration and synchronization are declared, replay obligations are preserved or residualized, and every defect of the bridge is emitted as a first-class token rather than hidden by coercion.}}]

Appendix N

Appendix O — Compiler Reference, PackSpec DSL, Deterministic Build Loop, and Publication Pipeline

Appendix O is the manuscript’s build constitution. It is not a generic implementation note and not a convenience appendix for software-adjacent readers. Its role is normative: it defines how a lawful pack is specified, how a lawful run is compiled, how ambiguity is branched without semantic drift, how regression and replay are enforced, how cross-pack handoffs are governed, and how publication becomes possible only as the terminal consequence of corridor-closed, replay-closed, policy-pinned execution. In the active corpus this role is explicit. Appendix O is named the compiler reference and publication-only appendix; compiler or build claims elsewhere are illegal unless they conform to it; and every publishable export is constrained to an OK-only dependency cone under pinned policies, pinned address derivation, pinned environment contracts, and replay capsules sufficient for an independent verifier to reconstruct the same OK outcomes.

The governing thesis of the appendix is therefore[\boxed{\text{A manuscript claim becomes a lawful built artifact if and only if it is produced by a typed PackSpec under a deterministic stage order, all corridor and truth gates are honored before scoring and publication, all branch and handoff events are ledgered, and the final export remains replayable as the same OK outcome under the pinned policy and environment.}}]

This thesis synthesizes two live corpus pressures that must be held together. The first is the compiler contract: the universe is treated as a build system in which a typed PackSpec and data produce a replayable ledger artifact with typed truth outcomes. The second is the publication contract: publication is not “sharing files,” but exporting a dependency-closed cone of OK nodes with no contradictory or unresolved states inside the authoritative manifest. Appendix O is where these two pressures become one executable law.

The primitive object of the appendix is the PackSpec. The live corpus already defines PackSpec as a typed DSL compiled to canonical JSON and resolved entirely by content-addressed references, with explicit required blocks and strong restrictions on defaults. Appendix O adopts that law in full. A lawful PackSpec is

[

\mathcal P

\big(\mathrm{DialSpecRef},\mathrm{LatticeSpecRef},\mathrm{AnchorSpecRef},\mathrm{PrimeRegistrySnapshotRef},\mathrm{DetectorRegistrySnapshotRef},\mathrm{ModeRegistrySnapshotRef},\mathrm{KernelSpecRef},\mathrm{SliceSpecRef},\mathrm{FlowSpecRef},\mathrm{CorridorSpecRef},\mathrm{LedgerSpecRef},\mathrm{MetricSpecRef},\mathrm{CompilerPolicyRef},\mathrm{PinsRef},\omega_{\mathcal P}\big),]with the understanding that (\mathrm{KernelSpecRef}) and (\mathrm{SliceSpecRef}) are required whenever the pack exposes face or (\tau)-sensitive behavior. Every block is content-addressed by ((\mathrm{id},\mathrm{version},\mathrm{hash})), and every referenced object is interpreted only through its pinned hash, never through a mutable name alone. This is not an optional design choice. The corpus treats it as the canonical compiler contract.

Appendix O imposes a hard completeness rule on the PackSpec. Let[\operatorname{Req}{\mathrm{Pack}}(\mathcal P)]be the required block set listed above. Then[\operatorname{PackLegal}(\mathcal P)=1\iff\forall b\in \operatorname{Req}{\mathrm{Pack}}(\mathcal P),\ b\ \text{is present, pinned, and schema-valid}.]This means there is no lawful “partial PackSpec” for any pack that makes public or cross-pack claims. Missing compiler inputs are not silently synthesized. They are build blockers. This is consistent with the active corpus’s explicit prohibition on omitted core blocks, especially those governing primary metrics, evidence provenance, corridor thresholds, and prime activation.

Defaults are permitted only under logged, pinned, and nonsemantic conditions. The corpus already states the rule sharply: defaults are legal only when the default source is registry-pinned, the compiler logs which fields were defaulted, and defaults do not apply to primary metrics, evidence provenance, corridor thresholds, or prime activation. Appendix O therefore defines a default application operator[\operatorname{Default}(\mathcal P,\mathcal R)\to(\mathcal P',\mathcal L_{\mathrm{def}})]that may succeed only if the default source registry (\mathcal R) is pinned and the emitted ledger (\mathcal L_{\mathrm{def}}) records every defaulted field. The legality law is[\operatorname{DefaultOK}=1\iff\mathrm{RegistryPinned}\land\mathrm{DefaultLogComplete}\land\mathrm{NoCriticalFieldDefaulted}.]This law prevents the build system from acquiring hidden semantic degrees of freedom under the appearance of convenience.

The second primitive object of the appendix is the stage graph. Appendix O is not merely a grammar appendix; it fixes the compile order. The active corpus repeatedly names the stage ordering and gives the pipeline as Parse (\to) Infer (\to) Gate (\to) Drift (\to) Score (\to) Ledger. Appendix O therefore defines the canonical stage graph

[

\mathfrak S_O

\big({\mathrm{Parse},\mathrm{Infer},\mathrm{Gate},\mathrm{Drift},\mathrm{Score},\mathrm{Emit}},E_O\big),]with edges[\mathrm{Parse}\to\mathrm{Infer}\to\mathrm{Gate}\to\mathrm{Drift}\to\mathrm{Score}\to\mathrm{Emit}.]The graph is acyclic, deterministic, and policy-pinned. The most important invariant is corridor-first separation:[\boxed{\text{No score may be computed, reported, or used for claim promotion until gating has succeeded under the active corridor.}}]The corpus already treats this as non-negotiable at the chapter level, and Appendix O is where it becomes the actual build law rather than a conceptual theorem.

The compile loop is therefore fixed as

[

\operatorname{Compile}(\mathcal P,\mathrm{Data})

\operatorname{Emit}\circ\operatorname{Score}\circ\operatorname{Drift}\circ\operatorname{Gate}\circ\operatorname{Infer}\circ\operatorname{Parse}(\mathcal P,\mathrm{Data}),]subject to early stop and branching laws. Let (o_{\mathrm{gate}}\in{\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}}) be the gate result. Then the active control law is:[o_{\mathrm{gate}}=\mathrm{FAIL}\Longrightarrow\text{stop immediately and emit failure ledger;}][o_{\mathrm{gate}}=\mathrm{AMBIG}\Longrightarrow\text{branch under explicit ambiguity policy and forbid direct publish;}][o_{\mathrm{gate}}\in{\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR}}\Longrightarrow\text{drift and score may proceed under policy and budgets.}]This is precisely the separation theorem and branch discipline already explicit in the chapter corpus and reiterated in the implementation materials. Appendix O specializes those rules into compiler mechanics.

The compiler must be deterministic under pins. Let

[

\mathcal E

\big(\mathrm{EnvPins},\mathrm{DataPins},\mathrm{SolverPins},\mathrm{NumericPins},\mathrm{TolerancePins},\mathrm{ReductionPins}\big)]be the active build environment contract. Then the determinism law is[(\mathcal P,\mathcal E,\mathrm{Data})\ \text{fixed}\Longrightarrow\operatorname{Compile}(\mathcal P,\mathrm{Data})\ \text{is single-valued up to canonical bytes}.]This means equal PackSpec, equal pins, and equal data produce equal stage artifacts, equal stage hashes, equal truth outcomes, and equal replay obligations. The corpus already states this as a global build invariant and makes deterministic replay one of Appendix O’s defining requirements.

To support this, Appendix O must define stage artifacts and stage hashes. Let the emitted stage family be

[

\mathcal A_O

{

A_{\mathrm{parse}},

A_{\mathrm{infer}},

A_{\mathrm{gate}},

A_{\mathrm{drift}},

A_{\mathrm{score}},

A_{\mathrm{emit}}

},

]

with each artifact canonically serialized and hashed. Then a lawful build emits the stage hash chain

[

h_{k+1}

H\big(h_k \Vert \operatorname{Can}(A_{k+1})\big).]This chain is part of the final ledger and part of the replay burden. The active corpus repeatedly ties PackSpec compilation, deterministic replay, stage ordering, and publication to stage hashes and certificate stacks, so Appendix O must treat this chain as normative rather than illustrative.

Because AppO is the build-system appendix, it must also define the dependency DAG. A pack’s dependency structure is not legal unless explicit and acyclic at publish time. Let

[

\mathcal G_{\mathrm{dep}}(\mathcal P)

(V_{\mathcal P},E_{\mathcal P})]be the dependency graph induced by the PackSpec’s referenced blocks and downstream imports. The legal-build law is[\operatorname{DepOK}(\mathcal P)=1\iff\mathcal G_{\mathrm{dep}}(\mathcal P)\ \text{is acyclic}]unless a cycle is broken through a declared hub abstraction and one direction is degraded from build-dependency to reference-only. This exact rule is already present in the chapter-side architecture law and is operationally required by AppO’s role as compiler reference.

Appendix O must further govern branching on ambiguity. The current corpus states explicitly that branching on AMBIG belongs to AppO and that conservative merge rules and publish rules under branching are part of its core. Appendix O therefore defines a branch ledger

[

\mathcal B_O

\big(\mathrm{BranchID},\mathrm{ParentRun},\mathrm{CandidateSet},\mathrm{BranchPolicy},\mathrm{MergePolicy},\mathrm{PublishPolicy},\omega_{\mathcal B}\big).]The branch law is:[o_{\mathrm{gate}}=\mathrm{AMBIG}\Longrightarrow\exists, \mathcal B_O]and no direct publish route is legal until one branch has been replay-closed and all other surviving branches have been either resolved, quarantined, or retained as typed ambiguity. This is the exact compiler-side realization of the typed truth and ambiguity laws.

Cross-pack handoffs also belong to Appendix O. The active corpus explicitly places handoff engines and pack transitions inside AppO, not in the corridor appendices alone. This means the compiler must know how a built artifact or typed state is handed from one pack to another without silent coercion. The canonical handoff packet is

[

\mathcal H_O

\big(\mathrm{SourcePack},\mathrm{TargetPack},\mathrm{Payload},\mathrm{InterfaceContract},\mathrm{TruthState},\mathrm{ReplayCapsule},\mathrm{MigrationData},\omega_{\mathcal H}\big).]The legality law is[\operatorname{HandoffOK}=1\iff\operatorname{InterfaceContractOK}\land\operatorname{TruthStateAllowed}\land\operatorname{ReplayCapsulePresent}\land\operatorname{NoSilentCoercion}.]This law is directly supported by the corpus’s insistence that AppO owns cross-pack handoffs and that such handoffs remain corridor-first, replay-bearing, and version-aware.

Discovery governance is another mandatory function of Appendix O. The live implementation texts route residual signatures and candidate discovery through AppO, but only after globality, minimality, anti-fit, and ablation gates are passed. Thus Appendix O must define the discovery admission record

[

\mathcal D_O

\big(\mathrm{ResidualSignature},\mathrm{CandidateChange},\mathrm{AblationSet},\mathrm{GovernanceGate},\mathrm{RollbackPlan},\omega_{\mathcal D}\big).]No proposed improvement may become part of a legal pack merely because it improves one score. It must satisfy the same compiler contract as any other change: one-change ablation, family-wide evidence, deterministic replay, and no per-instance tuning. This is a direct operational consequence of the current corpus’s upgrade law for CUT and of AppO’s position as the compiler-and-governance appendix.

Appendix O must also integrate with the broader appendix rail exactly as the live corpus specifies. Its deep integration list already names:

AppM for metrics and regression,

AppD and AppE for prime/detector evidence,

AppK and AppL for corridor algebra and typed truth,

AppH for bounded drift,

AppJ for mode bindings,

AppA for types and units.

This list is not descriptive. It is the dependency skeleton of the compiler. It means the compiler may not claim independence from metrics, drift, corridor, truth typing, or type/unit law. Every serious build in this system is therefore a coordinated appendix-level orchestration, and Appendix O is the conductor of that orchestration.

The publication pipeline is the final and most severe function of the appendix. The active corpus states the law in exact terms: publication is not “sharing files”; it is exporting a dependency-closed cone of OK nodes with pinned policies, pinned address derivation, pinned environment contract, and replay capsules sufficient for an independent verifier to reproduce the same OK outcomes. It also states four publication invariants: OK-only cone, no-CONFLICT cone, policy pinning, and address policy pinning. Appendix O therefore adopts the canonical publication bundle

[

\mathcal P_O

\big(\mathrm{BundleID},\mathrm{Manifest},\mathrm{DependencyCone},\mathrm{PolicyPins},\mathrm{AddressPolicyID},\mathrm{EnvContract},\mathrm{ReplayCapsules},\mathrm{Signatures},\omega_{\mathcal P}\big).]The export law is[\operatorname{PublishOK}(\mathcal P_O)=1\iff\operatorname{ConeTruth}=\mathrm{OK}\land\operatorname{NoConflictCone}\land\operatorname{PolicyPinsClosed}\land\operatorname{AddressPolicyPinned}\land\operatorname{ReplayCapsulesSufficient}.]Anything less is not publication. It is draft transport or internal staging. This exact law is already present in the active corpus and is the deepest reason Appendix O cannot be written as a generic compiler appendix.

The appendix must also define import discipline. A lawful import is not merely accepting a bundle with signatures. It is reconstructing the bundle under the pinned policy, pinned address derivation, and pinned replay capsules, and reproducing the same OK outcomes. Thus[\operatorname{ImportOK}(\mathcal P_O)=1\iff\operatorname{ManifestVerified}\land\operatorname{ReplayPass}\land\operatorname{PolicySatisfied}\land\operatorname{AddressPolicySatisfied}\land\operatorname{RevocationApplied}.]This protects the system against “compatible enough” imports that would silently shift semantics or proof strength.

The failure modes of Appendix O must also be typed. At minimum there are eight canonical compiler failures:

PackSpec incompleteness — required block missing or unpinned.

Illegal defaulting — default applied to forbidden field or unlogged source.

Dependency cycle breach — unresolved cycle in build DAG.

Gate-order breach — score or later stage executed before lawful gating.

Ambiguity laundering — branch suppressed or unpublished AMBIG forced into apparent OK.

Cross-pack coercion — handoff performed without legal interface contract.

Replay insufficiency — build artifact cannot be independently reconstructed.

Publication cone breach — NEAR, AMBIG, FAIL, or CONFLICT retained inside a supposedly publishable cone.

Each such failure must emit a typed ledger artifact, not a prose complaint, because Appendix O is itself a proof-carrying build law.

The final and deepest role of Appendix O is to make the manuscript executable as a civilization rather than only as a theorem object. Earlier appendices provide the crystals of address, law, kernel, truth, timing, corridor, value, replay, and interface. Appendix O is where those crystals are braided into a lawful build system that can parse, infer, gate, drift, score, ledger, branch, migrate, and publish without leaving the constitutional space of the manuscript. That is why it stands so late in the appendix ring. It is not primitive law. It is operational law in full.

In compressed form, the governing law of Appendix O may be written as[\boxed{\text{A manuscript build is lawful if and only if a fully specified PackSpec compiles under deterministic stage order, corridor-first gating, explicit branch and handoff laws, replay-bearing ledgers, and policy-pinned publication rules, such that an independent verifier can reconstruct the same OK dependency cone without silent coercion or omitted obligations.}}]

Appendix O

Appendix Q — Appendix-Only Integrated Metro Map, Hub Lattice, and Reentry Civilization

Appendix Q is not one appendix among the others. It is the appendix field seen as a civilization. Appendix A gives entry and address. Appendix B gives law. Appendix C gives finite kernel and route algebra. Appendix D gives constitutional truth typing. Appendix E gives clock and release cadence. Appendix F gives corridor admissibility. Appendix G gives executable fire packets. Appendix H gives feasibility and detector topology. Appendix I gives truth corridors and verdict frames. Appendix J gives bounded residual work. Appendix K gives quarantine and reentry from failure. Appendix L gives verifier kernel and bundle layouts. Appendix M gives replay sovereignty and archive closure. Appendix N governs interfaces, boundaries, and exchange. Appendix O governs compilation and publication. Appendix P turns the whole chapter corpus into an arc atlas and orbiting whole. Appendix Q is the appendix-only integrated metro nexus in which all of those appendices become one navigable, replayable, bounded, and reentrant field. The live corpus is explicit on this point: Appendix Q is the “appendix-only integration map,” the “appendix-only metro map,” and the appendix-side civilization whose task is to expose the full A–P appendix crystal as a lawful route system rather than a list of supplements.

The governing thesis of the appendix is therefore[\boxed{\text{The appendix field is lawfully complete only when the appendices A–P are compiled into one deterministic metro whose nodes, hubs, corridors, budgets, truth rails, replay rails, governance rails, and chapter reentry lines are all explicit, replay-verifiable, and closed under the same seed-preserving return law as the main manuscript body.}}]

This thesis is stronger than saying “the appendices are connected.” It says the appendix field has its own zero point, its own lines, its own transfer hubs, its own route constraints, its own dependency algebra, and its own reentry law into the chapter body. The appendix field is therefore not subordinate commentary. It is a second body of the manuscript: a denser infrastructural crystal whose primary function is to support lawful retrieval, lawful implementation, lawful repair, lawful publication, and lawful return. The active corpus repeatedly forces exactly this interpretation by asking that the appendix-only metro map feel like a complete appendix-side civilization rather than a small extra note and by embedding Appendix Q as the fully integrated appendix nexus of the larger crystal.

The primitive object of Appendix Q is the appendix metro graph[\mathcal M_Q=(V_Q,E_Q),]where[V_Q={\mathrm{AppA},\mathrm{AppB},\dots,\mathrm{AppP}}]is the full node atlas of the sixteen appendices and (E_Q) is the typed edge set of lawful appendix-to-appendix routes. An appendix edge is never a generic “related to” relation. It must be one of a small bounded family of metro edge classes:[\mathfrak E_Q={\mathrm{FOUND},\mathrm{ROUTE},\mathrm{WIT},\mathrm{REPLAY},\mathrm{GOV},\mathrm{BUILD},\mathrm{PUBLISH},\mathrm{RETURN}}.]These mean respectively: foundational dependence, routing dependence, witness/truth dependence, replay/verification dependence, governance dependence, compiler/build dependence, publication dependence, and chapter/body return dependence. This law is consistent with the active appendix corpus because the appendices we drafted from live files are already role-separated exactly along these lines, and the appendix-only map prompts require explicit clusters, transfer hubs, dependencies, and reentry routes rather than vague thematic grouping.

The first invariant of the appendix-only metro is node completeness:[|V_Q|=16]with no missing stations and no hidden “meta appendix” outside the map. Appendix Q itself is not a seventeenth appendix; it is the authoritative map object that integrates the A–P field. Thus the node atlas is fixed as follows.

[\begin{aligned}\mathrm{AppA}&:\text{ Address Registry / namespace / collision resolution},\\mathrm{AppB}&:\text{ Law Library / admissibility axioms / proof obligations},\\mathrm{AppC}&:\text{ Kernel Calculus / primitive route grammar / index algebra},\\mathrm{AppD}&:\text{ Truth Spine / constitutional proofs / failure packet law},\\mathrm{AppE}&:\text{ Circle Gear / mixed-radix clock / dynamic scheduling},\\mathrm{AppF}&:\text{ Corridor Algebra / truth typing / requiredness maps},\\mathrm{AppG}&:\text{ Fire Arc Hub / recipe packets / dosage / tria prima control},\\mathrm{AppH}&:\text{ Feasibility Spine / detector catalog / coupling topology},\\mathrm{AppI}&:\text{ Truth Corridors / verdict frames / }\Sigma\text{-truth spine},\\mathrm{AppJ}&:\text{ NEAR Workbench / residual ledgers / simulation corridors},\\mathrm{AppK}&:\text{ Quarantined Void / failure packets / reentry law},\\mathrm{AppL}&:\text{ Verifier Kernel / replay formats / bundle layouts},\\mathrm{AppM}&:\text{ Replay Hub / deterministic reruns / rebuild proofs},\\mathrm{AppN}&:\text{ Interfaces / boundaries / exchange formats / compatibility},\\mathrm{AppO}&:\text{ Compiler Reference / PackSpec DSL / publication pipeline},\\mathrm{AppP}&:\text{ Arc Atlas / orbit closure / cross-arc weaving / index spines}.\end{aligned}]This node atlas is not speculative; it is the reconciled live role set of the appendices drafted against the current corpus. Appendix Q’s first duty is to freeze this as the canonical appendix station table.

The second invariant is the four-row crystal arrangement. The live appendix metro snippets repeatedly expose a 4×4 field, beginning explicitly with[\mathrm{AppA}\to \mathrm{AppE}\to \mathrm{AppI}\to \mathrm{AppM},\qquad\mathrm{AppB}\to \mathrm{AppF}\to \mathrm{AppJ}\to \mathrm{AppN},]and strongly implying the continued 4×4 appendix crystal. Appendix Q therefore formalizes the row-major appendix lattice as[\begin{matrix}\mathrm{AppA} & \mathrm{AppE} & \mathrm{AppI} & \mathrm{AppM}\\mathrm{AppB} & \mathrm{AppF} & \mathrm{AppJ} & \mathrm{AppN}\\mathrm{AppC} & \mathrm{AppG} & \mathrm{AppK} & \mathrm{AppO}\\mathrm{AppD} & \mathrm{AppH} & \mathrm{AppL} & \mathrm{AppP}\end{matrix}]with the understanding that rows and columns are not decorative layout but traffic-bearing channels. This arrangement is the cleanest synthesis of the current live appendix roles with the crystal snippets in the corpus. It preserves the strong first two rows explicitly visible in the source and places the remaining appendices in a way that respects the functional progression from kernel and truth through failure and replay to publication and atlas closure. The arrangement must therefore be treated as a canonical appendix-side station grid unless superseded by a later pinned migration.

From that crystal arrangement, Appendix Q defines four primary horizontal lines.

The Entry/Truth/Replay line[\mathrm{AppA}\to \mathrm{AppE}\to \mathrm{AppI}\to \mathrm{AppM}]is the mandatory support spine seen in its wider Flower-side expansion. AppA seats objects, AppE times them, AppI corridor-types them, and AppM reruns and rebuilds them. This line is the appendix field’s minimal survivable epistemic backbone.

The Law/Corridor/Residual/Boundary line[\mathrm{AppB}\to \mathrm{AppF}\to \mathrm{AppJ}\to \mathrm{AppN}]is the bounded-incompleteness and compatibility rail. Law generates corridor discipline; corridor discipline yields bounded residual work; bounded residual work eventually requires explicit interface and migration governance. This line is the appendix field’s legal and interfacial middle nervous rail.

The Kernel/Execution/Failure/Build line[\mathrm{AppC}\to \mathrm{AppG}\to \mathrm{AppK}\to \mathrm{AppO}]is the execution rail. Finite structural movement becomes recipe execution; recipe execution encounters hard failure and quarantine when it breaks; successful resolution or exclusion of those failures is a prerequisite for lawful build and publication. This line is the field’s operational risk rail.

The Proof/Feasibility/Verification/Atlas line[\mathrm{AppD}\to \mathrm{AppH}\to \mathrm{AppL}\to \mathrm{AppP}]is the topological and certification rail. Constitutional proof constrains feasibility; feasibility constrains verification; verification constrains atlas closure and global navigability. This line is the field’s constitutional map rail.

These lines are the primary appendix-only metro lines. They are already latent in the active corpus and now made explicit as law.

The third invariant of Appendix Q is the transfer-hub system. The appendix field is not merely four parallel lines; it has major interchange points that route between them. The most important transfer hubs are as follows.

HQ₀ — Zero and replay hub[{\mathrm{AppA},\mathrm{AppI},\mathrm{AppM}}]This is the appendix-side equivalent of the mandatory chapter support skeleton. It is the smallest triad through which all strong epistemic routes must pass.

HQ₁ — Law and bounded work hub[{\mathrm{AppB},\mathrm{AppF},\mathrm{AppJ}}]This hub governs admissibility, residual work, and bounded upgrade.

HQ₂ — Feasibility and verification hub[{\mathrm{AppD},\mathrm{AppH},\mathrm{AppL}}]This hub governs constitutional truth packets, defect detection, and replay verification.

HQ₃ — Execution and publication hub[{\mathrm{AppC},\mathrm{AppG},\mathrm{AppO}}]This hub governs kernel execution, fire-side control, and lawful build/export.

HQ₄ — Boundary and atlas hub[{\mathrm{AppN},\mathrm{AppP}}]This hub governs compatibility governance and the final map of the whole manuscript.

HQ₅ — Failure sink hub[{\mathrm{AppK}}]This is the unique quarantine sink and therefore a one-node transfer hub of special class.

Every appendix-side route is required to declare its hub passage explicitly. This keeps the field deterministic and retrievable.

The fourth invariant is dependency ordering. The appendix-only metro is not acyclic in the sense of one-way dependency, because it must support replay, repair, and reentry loops, but it does carry a canonical dependency partial order.
